1548014402825 UID: 375967251804848128 CID: 480844958287396876 U: Tatourmi Msg: The Powerful and the Worthless:

You may not gain any prestige from an empire which has more than three points of prestige less than you. If such an empire forces you into a prestige wager and loses, you inflict a crisis on them instead of stealing one of their prestige points. They literally have nothing that would significantly help you in your quest to rule this world.

The Final Battle:
    
In any prestige wager involving an empire with nine prestige in which that empire can reach 10, the restriction on the maximum number of traits that can effectively be used in a wager do not apply. Enjoy the carnage. Evt: [object Object]
1548014409777 UID: 375967251804848128 CID: 480844958287396876 U: Tatourmi Msg: Writing History:

If your empire reaches 10 prestige (Either by yourself or by combining your score with the one of your vassals), you did it. You cemented your place as the most powerful empire on the face of earth and you will rule these lands… For a time.

Your first order of business is to contact the moderators: Make sure they spread words of your glory far and wide, then, it’s time to get to work!

Once you reach 10 prestige, the whole rp switches modes for a time. We zoom away from the daily struggles of our characters and we take a broader look at history itself. For a duration of your choosing, but up to a maximum of ten years, we will not play our characters directly. Every empire leader will instead describe how their empire fared during this time in a process which we will call “The Interlude”

You may, exceptionally, make something with potentially lasting implications happen to the world itself. Every other player will be forced to include it in their own interlude. You may not target any specific player and say “Your empire is destroyed”, but you may say “This is a time for revolts, and the colonies thirst for freedom” or “Massive storms engulf the skies. Airships are left behind”. Evt: [object Object]
1548014417291 UID: 375967251804848128 CID: 480844958287396876 U: Tatourmi Msg: This event, which we will call a “hook” will be the driving force behind each and every interlude, and it will be your contribution to history itself. Pick well!

Once you have picked the hook, every empire will write their interlude, which will describe how their empire evolved during this time period. You, as the empire which reached 10, do not have any restrictions. You rule the world now, you can write whatever you want, no strings attached. Other empire leaders do not have the same luxury. They can also write their own story freely, but they will need to include a few things in their interlude depending on how much prestige they have.

If your empire has 9 or 8 prestige, you must include something negative related to the key. You were prepared for everything but that, and history isn’t kind to second-bests. Give one of your prestige points to the people with the lowest score. You may pick if there is a tie.
If your empire has 7, 6, 5 or 4 prestige, you must include something negative and something positive tied to the key. It’s life.
If your empire has 3, 2 or 1 prestige, you must include something positive related to the key. You may also steal one prestige from someone else of your choice if you haven’t received anything from the top dogs already. Things weren’t looking great, but you took advantage of that opportunity. This world will change.

But all things have to come to an end. After every golden age comes a great crisis. 
Describe your empire’s downfall and divide your lands. You may keep two-thirds, lose prestige until you have 6 and give it, along with some of your old lands, to any players of your choice with 5 or less prestige. The rats feast on the remains of the kings of old. Evt: [object Object]

- I also have the `roll` command, it works as a automatic 2d6 if you don't add comments

there are a bunch of other things in the works

1548018746613 UID: 517269535024349195 CID: 481133060348182550 U: Molten Greebel Msg: `Random lore!:` **SpinGrad** 
------------------------------------------------
[backstory]: Spinning `Ubergrad`(Spingrad)

_once upon a time, a certain `Molten` created madman, made for eradicating gods and so-called 'devine' decided to randomly mess around with a country using a randomly picked method of torment, in this case it was `Ubergrad`, a unlucky empire who was just minding its own business. the method what the torment was "moving ground", `the Joker`(sometimes referred under similar names or as `The Exiled` by the `Molten` themselves) then made this happen to `Ubergrad`, constantly, day and night.

the ores were formed into machinery, the ground was split apart with precision, the water flowed down under the plates and as the heat flowed  into the machines the "plates" started to turn... and turn they did, now the capital is the only city in the world to face the west, north and east coast of its borders on a given day.

after much deliberation they made a drill machine dig down into one of the plates, after a long time(several KM's) they made their way into a machine room... the place was covered in darkness and everything in the unseen space was moving with cogs and gears, moving bands of metal and steel... the expedition eventually made their way into the center where there was a control hub, they did so however at a cost of losing many limbs, no casualties, and a loss of sanity for a few of them. the plate they were on was stopped only after the creator of them showed up to rave and rant and decided to stop it himself._

1548026117535 UID: 367088742189629440 CID: 505365061959680000 U: The Mad Doktor Msg: ```THE CURRENT RULES OF MAGIC```

`THAUMATURGIC UNITS`
We will be using Manic Units, or for the sake of brevity abbreviated to MU, to describe magical value. These will regenerate over time depending on Magical Level, and may be spent to accomplish thaumic reactions. Having insufficient Mana will simply make the reaction fail to occur without a roll.

`THE LAW OF EQUIVALENT EXCHANGE`
In our instance of this, MU will equate to 1 Metric unit (MeUn). I.E:
1 Kilogram ***transmutated*** will cost 1 MU.
1 (Whatever the fuck liquid units are in your weird european nonsense) ***transmuted*** will cost 1 MU.
1 KiloNewton ***applied*** (In a specific vector) will cost 1 MU.
And so on. 

`THAUMATURGIC PROGRESSION`
In order to become a Thaumaturge or ascend in the progression system, you must accomplish 1 of 3 things. 1 action is non-applicable until the level of `Sourcerer` is achieved.
1: You may become the 7th born in a generation, granting you 1 Magical classification upward. Being the 7th born makes you a `Scribe`. Being the 7th born of a 7th born makes you a `Wizard`. Being the 7th born of a 7th born of a 7th born makes you a `Sourcerer`.

2: You may experience a deeply personal and incredibly traumatic event playing upon your very soul, to ascend 1 magical level. This event must be clearly (and preferably gruesomely) described in detail. For example:
Character's worst fears come to pass and their entire way of life is destroyed, +1 level.
Doing this will get you up to `Sourcerer`.

3: Upon reaching the level of `Sourcerer` is this only feasible, unless in a group. When you collect 6 `SOUL`s and amalgamate them into your own, the resulting power will have you instantly ascend to the classification `Eldritch`. Snatching and Amalgamating 1 soul will cost you `140 MU`, `70` to rip it from the host, `70` more to absorb it.

(Too much text, typing in multiple parts) Evt: [object Object]

1548026541697 UID: 295652009745448971 CID: 517303057676238851 U: Vabese Msg: $addlore reason-Lancre
"According to folk myth and legend deciphered from machine written texts, the tale of the Isle of `Lancre` involves a crescent shaped land-mass with blue green grass, home to only one individual. `The Nobody`. The texts describe his face as being unable to be remembered, and the `black raven` which accompanies him is theorized by the original authors to be one of Death's manifestations. One sunny afternoon, `the Nobody` activates some sort of hidden device within the island, speculated by mythologists to be either magical or some sort of incredibly complex clockwork. The work states that: "Upon the 17th minute of the 17th hour, `Lancre` rose upon 7 slender, bronze legs to journey the sea, never to be seen again." Topography maps have confirmed a deep depression in the Southern Sea matching `Lancre`'s supposed shape, although the entire island is missing from all maps and witnesses are none. The identity of `The Nobody` appears to be an extremely dangerous and highly secret bit of knowledge, as many an informant was killed by unknown means after giving us a section of text. All that remains to be found out is the identity of `the raven`, `the man`, and the location of this legendary landmass." Evt: [object Object]

1548026598590 UID: 367088742189629440 CID: 505365061959680000 U: The Mad Doktor Msg: ```SECTION 2```

`THAUAMTURGIC CLASSIFICATIONS`
There are 4 levels of Magical ability. Below their numerics are detailed.

*Scribes*
Magical Capacity = 7 MU (Manic Units)
Regeneration = 7 MU/1 Hr

*Wizards*
Magical Capacity = 7^2 MU
Regeneration = 70 MU/1 Hr

*Sourcerers*
Magical Capacity = (7^2)^3 MU
Regeneration = 700 MU/1 Hr

*Eldritch*
Magical Capacity: ((7^2)^3)^4 MU
Regeneration = 7,000 MU/1 Hr

`ON MAKING MAGICAL CHARACTERS`
Creating a magical player character will instill 2 Debuffs on the empire housing them.  The Prestige debuff will simply mean that in the ledger they technically can only operate with up to 8 actual prestige, and the prestige lost in the creation of the character will still apply upon reaching `10`. If they do not canonically belong to any empire, they will instill 2 Debuffs on the player's faction in general.  `SCRIBES` cost 1 Empire Currency, as they are the first Magical Level. They do not remove Prestige. `WIZARDS` cost 2 Empire Currency, as they are the second ML. They mechanically lower Prestige by 1. `SOURCERERS` cost 3 Empire Currency, as they are the third ML. They mechanically lower Prestige by 2. `Eldritch` characters cannot be bought and must be 'levelled up' IRP, by aforementioned methodologies. They mechanically lower Prestige by 4, due to sheer power. Evt: [object Object]
